Reads code.json to find:\n        - first instruction index in loop\n        - first instruction index in epilogue\n        - hitcounts to compute number of iterations\n  2. Processes se0_sm0_sl0_wv*.json files.\n  3. Reports per-wave durations, average loop duration,\n     and average duration per iteration.\n\"\"\"\n\nimport argparse\nimport json\nimport os\nimport re\nimport sys\nfrom glob import glob\n\n# MFMA instruction cycle mapping for non-scaled versions\nMFMA_CYCLE_MAP = {\n    \"v_mfma_f32_16x16x32_f16\": 16,\n    \"v_mfma_f32_32x32x16_f16\": 32,\n    # Add more scaled MFMA instructions as needed\n}\n\n\ndef extract_cbsz_blgp(instruction):\n    \"\"\"\n    Extract cbsz and blgp values from an MFMA instruction.\n\n    Args:\n        instruction: String containing the MFMA instruction\n\n    Returns:\n        tuple: (cbsz_value, blgp_value) or (None, None) if not found\n    \"\"\"\n    cbsz_match = re.search(r\"cbsz:(\\d+)\", instruction)\n    blgp_match = re.search(r\"blgp:(\\d+)\", instruction)\n\n    cbsz = int(cbsz_match.group(1)) if cbsz_match else None\n    blgp = int(blgp_match.group(1)) if blgp_match else None\n\n    return cbsz, blgp\n\n\ndef get_mfma_opcode(instruction):\n    \"\"\"\n    Extract the MFMA opcode from the instruction.\n\n    Args:\n        instruction: String containing the MFMA instruction\n\n    Returns:\n        str: The opcode (e.g., \"v_mfma_f32_16x16x32_f16\")\n    \"\"\"\n    # Match pattern like \"v_mfma_...\" up to the first space or end\n    match = re.match(r\"(v_mfma_\\S+?)(?:\\s|$)\", instruction.strip())\n    if match:\n        return match.group(1)\n    return None\n\n\ndef get_mfma_cycles(instruction):\n    \"\"\"\n    Determine the cycle count for an MFMA instruction.\n\n    Args:\n        instruction: String containing the MFMA instruction\n\n    Returns:\n        int: Number of cycles for the instruction, or 0 if not an MFMA\n    \"\"\"\n    instruction_lower = instruction.lower()\n\n    # Check if it's an MFMA instruction\n    if \"v_mfma\" not in instruction_lower:\n        return 0\n\n    # Extract the opcode\n    opcode = get_mfma_opcode(instruction_lower)\n    if not opcode:\n        return 0\n\n    # Check if it's a scaled MFMA instruction\n    is_scale = \"v_mfma_scale\" in opcode\n\n    if is_scale:\n        # Find matching rule in MFMA_SCALE_CYCLE_RULES\n        matching_rule = None\n        for rule_opcode in MFMA_SCALE_CYCLE_RULES:\n            if rule_opcode in opcode:\n                matching_rule = rule_opcode\n                break\n\n        if not matching_rule:\n            # Unknown scaled MFMA, return 0 or a default value\n            print(f\"Warning: Unknown scaled MFMA instruction: {opcode}\", file=sys.stderr)\n            return 0\n\n        # Extract cbsz and blgp values\n        cbsz, blgp = extract_cbsz_blgp(instruction_lower)\n\n        # Apply the rule: if either cbsz or blgp is <= 1\n        rule = MFMA_SCALE_CYCLE_RULES[matching_rule]\n        if (cbsz is not None and cbsz <= 1) or (blgp is not None and blgp <= 1):\n            return rule[\"cbsz_or_blgp_le_1\"]\n        else:\n            return rule[\"default\"]\n\n    else:\n        # Non-scaled MFMA instruction\n        # Try to find exact match in the cycle map\n        if opcode in MFMA_CYCLE_MAP:\n            return MFMA_CYCLE_MAP[opcode]\n\n        # If not found, try to infer from dimensions\n        # Pattern: v_mfma_<type>_<M>x<N>x<K>_<input_type>\n        match = re.search(r\"v_mfma_\\w+_(\\d+)x(\\d+)x\\d+\", opcode)\n        if match:\n            m_dim = int(match.group(1))\n            n_dim = int(match.group(2))\n            # Typically, cycle count equals max(M, N)\n            cycles = max(m_dim, n_dim)\n            print(f\"Warning: Inferred cycles for {opcode}: {cycles}\", file=sys.stderr)\n            return cycles\n\n        # Unknown MFMA instruction\n        print(f\"Warning: Unknown MFMA instruction: {opcode}\", file=sys.stderr)\n        return 0\n\n\ndef load_code_json(folder):\n    path = os.path.join(folder, \"code.json\")\n    if not os.path.isfile(path):\n        raise FileNotFoundError(f\"code.json not found in {folder}\")\n    with open(path, \"r\", encoding=\"utf-8\") as f:\n        data = json.load(f)\n    if isinstance(data, dict) and \"code\" in data:\n        return data[\"code\"]\n    if isinstance(data, list):\n        return data\n    raise ValueError(\"Unexpected code.json format\")\n\n\ndef find_loop_branch(sorted_code):\n    \"\"\"Find the inner-loop back-edge.\n\n    Picks an s_cbranch instruction with the maximum hitcount among all\n    cbranches; among those, prefers one whose target jumps backward. AMDGPU\n    s_cbranch* encodes its target as a 16-bit signed relative offset, which\n    code.json surfaces as an unsigned integer in the instruction name (e.g.\n    `s_cbranch_execz 64855` means offset -681). A back-edge always has a\n    negative offset, so unsigned > 32767. Ties broken by program order\n    (last wins) so that, when the only cbranches are mid-loop guards, we\n    still land on the latest one — closest to the actual back-edge.\n\n    This handles three kernel shapes that the simpler \"first s_cbranch_scc\"\n    rule got wrong:\n      - v5_local_prefetch: early-out scc branches before the loop steal\n        precedence over the real back-edge, producing mfma_count_in_loop=0.\n      - v0_naive / v2_async_copy: many in-loop s_cbranch_execz mask-load\n        branches share the back-edge's hitcount, and the back-edge itself\n        is also an execz (not an scc).\n\n    Returns the position of the chosen branch in sorted_code, or None.\n    \"\"\"\n    cbranches = [\n        (i, ins) for i, ins in enumerate(sorted_code) if ins[0].lower().startswith(\"s_cbranch_\")\n    ]\n    if not cbranches:\n        return None\n\n    max_hit = max(ins[6] for _, ins in cbranches)\n    top = [(i, ins) for i, ins in cbranches if ins[6] == max_hit]\n\n    def is_backward(ins):\n        parts = ins[0].split()\n        if len(parts) < 2:\n            return False\n        try:\n            return int(parts[1]) > 32767\n        except ValueError:\n            return False\n\n    backward = [(i, ins) for i, ins in top if is_backward(ins)]\n    if backward:\n        return backward[-1][0]\n    return top[-1][0]\n\n\ndef analyze_code(code_list):\n    \"\"\"Extract loop info and compute iteration count.\"\"\"\n    sorted_code = sorted(code_list, key=lambda x: x[2])\n    hitcounts = [ins[6] for ins in sorted_code]\n    indices = [ins[2] for ins in sorted_code]\n    names = [ins[0] for ins in sorted_code]  # Keep original case for instruction parsing\n\n    # Primary method: find loop boundary via s_cbranch (back-edge).\n    # The instruction after the branch is the first epilogue instruction.\n    branch_pos = find_loop_branch(sorted_code)\n\n    if branch_pos is not None:\n        # Use branch-based loop detection\n        loop_hit = hitcounts[branch_pos]\n        # Loop starts at the first instruction with the same hitcount\n        loop_first_pos = next(i for i, h in enumerate(hitcounts) if h == loop_hit)\n        loop_last_pos = branch_pos\n        # Epilogue starts at the first post-back-edge instruction whose\n        # hitcount is below the loop's but still nonzero. Plain \"branch_pos\n        # + 1\" lands on dead code (hit=0) or trailing in-loop instructions\n        # (hit == loop_hit) for kernels like v0_naive whose back-edge has\n        # masked-load fall-through.\n        epilogue_first_pos = None\n        for j in range(branch_pos + 1, len(hitcounts)):\n            if 0 < hitcounts[j] < loop_hit:\n                epilogue_first_pos = j\n                break\n    else:\n        # Fallback: hitcount-based detection\n        max_hit = max(hitcounts)\n        loop_first_pos = next(i for i, h in enumerate(hitcounts) if h == max_hit)\n        loop_last_pos = max(i for i, h in enumerate(hitcounts) if h == max_hit)\n        epilogue_first_pos = loop_last_pos + 1 if loop_last_pos + 1 < len(hitcounts) else None\n\n    # Compute iterations: hitcount_loop / hitcount_epilogue\n    loop_hit = hitcounts[loop_first_pos]\n    if epilogue_first_pos is not None:\n        epilogue_hit = hitcounts[epilogue_first_pos]\n    else:\n        epilogue_hit = 0\n\n    if epilogue_hit == 0:\n        # No epilogue executed (dead code) - loop_hit is the iteration count\n        num_iterations = loop_hit\n        epilogue_first_index = None\n    else:\n        num_iterations = loop_hit / epilogue_hit\n        epilogue_first_index = indices[epilogue_first_pos]\n\n    # Count MFMA instructions and their total cycles in the loop\n    total_mfma_cycles = 0\n    mfma_count = 0\n    for i in range(loop_first_pos, loop_last_pos + 1):\n        cycles = get_mfma_cycles(names[i])\n        if cycles > 0:\n            mfma_count += 1\n            total_mfma_cycles += cycles\n\n    return {\n        \"loop_first_index\": indices[loop_first_pos],\n        \"loop_last_index\": indices[loop_last_pos],\n        \"epilogue_first_index\": epilogue_first_index,\n        \"mfma_count_in_loop\": mfma_count,\n        \"total_mfma_cycles_in_loop\": total_mfma_cycles,\n        \"loop_hitcount\": loop_hit,\n        \"epilogue_hitcount\": epilogue_hit,\n        \"num_iterations\": num_iterations,\n    }\n\n\ndef process_wave_file(path, loop_index, epilogue_index, loop_last_index=None):\n    \"\"\"Find first occurrence clocks in a wave JSON file.\n\n    Returns (prologue_duration, loop_duration, epilogue_duration, wave_iterations)\n    where wave_iterations is the number of loop iterations observed in this wave\n    (only set in no-epilogue mode, None otherwise).\n    \"\"\"\n    with open(path, \"r\", encoding=\"utf-8\") as f:\n        data = json.load(f)\n    if \"wave\" not in data or \"instructions\" not in data[\"wave\"]:\n        return None\n\n    instructions = data[\"wave\"][\"instructions\"]\n    loop_clock = None\n    epilogue_clock = None\n    wave_iterations = None\n\n    if epilogue_index is not None:\n        # Normal case: find first occurrence of loop and epilogue indices\n        for clock, _, _, _, idx in instructions:\n            if loop_clock is None and idx == loop_index:\n                loop_clock = clock\n            if epilogue_clock is None and idx == epilogue_index:\n                epilogue_clock = clock\n            if loop_clock is not None and epilogue_clock is not None:\n                break\n    else:\n        # No-epilogue case: find first occurrence of loop start, last\n        # occurrence of any instruction in the loop range as loop end,\n        # and count iterations by counting occurrences of loop_index.\n        last_loop_clock = None\n        iter_count = 0\n        for clock, _, _, _, idx in instructions:\n            if idx == loop_index:\n                if loop_clock is None:\n                    loop_clock = clock\n                iter_count += 1\n            if loop_index <= idx <= loop_last_index:\n                last_loop_clock = clock\n        epilogue_clock = last_loop_clock\n        wave_iterations = iter_count\n\n    start_clock = instructions[0][0]\n    end_clock = instructions[-1][0]\n\n    if loop_clock is None or epilogue_clock is None:\n        return None\n\n    pro = loop_clock - start_clock\n    epi = end_clock - epilogue_clock\n\n    return pro, epilogue_clock - loop_clock, epi, wave_iterations\n\n\ndef analyze_waves(folder, loop_index, epilogue_index, loop_last_index=None):\n    \"\"\"Process se*_sm0_sl0_wv*.json files and compute durations + average.\n\n    The leading shader-engine index can vary by GPU — runs on GPU 0 produce\n    se0_*, runs on other GPUs may produce se1_* / se2_* / etc. We glob across\n    all SE indices and use whichever SM0 wave files the ATT decoder wrote.\n    \"\"\"\n    pattern = os.path.join(folder, \"se*_sm0_sl0_wv*.json\")\n    files = sorted(glob(pattern))\n    if not files:\n        raise FileNotFoundError(f\"No files matching {pattern}\")\n\n    durations = {}\n    pro_dur = {}\n    epi_dur = {}\n    wave_iters = []\n    for path in files:\n        result = process_wave_file(path, loop_index, epilogue_index, loop_last_index)\n        if result is not None:\n            pro, dur, epi, w_iters = result\n            durations[os.path.basename(path)] = dur\n            pro_dur[os.path.basename(path)] = pro\n            epi_dur[os.path.basename(path)] = epi\n            if w_iters is not None:\n                wave_iters.append(w_iters)\n\n    if not durations:\n        raise ValueError(\"No valid loop durations found in any se*_sm0_sl0_wv*.json file\")\n\n    avg_duration = sum(durations.values()) / len(durations)\n    avg_pro_dur = sum(pro_dur.values()) / len(pro_dur)\n    avg_epi_dur = sum(epi_dur.values()) / len(epi_dur)\n    avg_wave_iters = sum(wave_iters) / len(wave_iters) if wave_iters else None\n    return durations, avg_duration, pro_dur, avg_pro_dur, epi_dur, avg_epi_dur, avg_wave_iters\n\n\ndef main():\n    parser = argparse.ArgumentParser(\n        description=\"Compute average loop and per-iteration durations.\"\n    )\n    parser.add_argument(\"folder\", help=\"Folder containing code.json and se0_sm0_sl0_wv*.json files\")\n    args = parser.parse_args()\n\n    try:\n        code_list = load_code_json(args.folder)\n        code_info = analyze_code(code_list)\n\n        durations,      code_info[\"loop_last_index\"],\n        )\n\n        # Use wave-derived iteration count when epilogue hitcount is 0\n        num_iterations = code_info[\"num_iterations\"]\n        if wave_iters Same structure as\n57:     a16w16/v8_sliceMN but with BF8 (e5m2) numerics and a16w16/v9-style\n58:     XCD-aware PID remapping.\n59: \n60:     The output tile is split into a 2x2 grid of quadrants:\n61: \n62:         C_tl  C_tr\n63:         C_bl  C_br\n64: \n65:     A is sliced along M into a_top / a_bot, B is sliced along N into\n66:     b_left / b_right. Each K-step runs four regions (one MFMA + one LR +\n67:     one AC each). The loop is unrolled by 2 so buffer indices alternate\n68:     naturally without runtime computation.\n69: \n70:     Address optimization: pre-compute two sets of offsets — base for even\n71: Same structure as\n    a16w16/v8_sliceMN but with BF8 (e5m2) numerics and a16w16/v9-style\n    XCD-aware PID remapping.\n\n    The output tile is split into a 2x2 grid of quadrants:\n\n        C_tl  C_tr\n        C_bl  C_br\n\n    A is sliced along M into a_top / a_bot, B is sliced along N into\n    b_left / b_right. The loop is unrolled by 2 so buffer indices alternate\n    naturally without runtime computation.\n\n    Address optimization: pre-compute two sets of offsets — base for even\n    K-steps and _next (shifted by BLOCK_K) for odd K-steps. a_base/b_base\n    advance by 2*BLOCK_K once per unrolled iteration.\n    \"\"\"\n\n    pid_m, pid_n = get_pids(M, N, BLOCK_M, BLOCK_N, GRID_MN, NUM_XCDS, 123.456\n    We grab the last float on the last such data row.\n    \"\"\"\n    tflops = None\n    for line in output.splitlines():\n        # Match pandas-style data rows: index followed by M, N, K floats and TFLOPS\n        m = re.match(r\"\\s*\\d+\\s+([\\d.]+\\s+[\\d.]+\\s+[\\d.]+\\s+.+)\", line)\n        if m:\n            nums = re.findall(r\"[\\d.]+\", m.group(1))\n            if nums:\n                tflops = float(nums[-1])\n    return tflops\n\n\ndef parse_mfma_efficiency(output):\n    \"\"\"Parse MFMA efficiency from process_json.py JSON output.\"\"\"\n    m = re.search(r'\"mfma file in triton cache.\"\"\"\n    pattern = os.path.join(TRITON_CACHE, \"*\", f\"{version_dir}*.amdgcn\")\n    files = glob.glob(pattern)\n    if not files:\n        return None, None\n\n    vgprs = int(sm.group(1))\n                if vgprs is not None and spills is not None:\n                    break\n        if vgprs is not None:\n            break\n\n    return vgprs, spills\n\n\ndef   # Return the most recently modified one\n    return max(files, key=os.path.getmtime)\n\n\ndef avg_kernel_time_ns(csv_path, kernel_name, last_n=100):\n    \"\"\"Return the average elapsed time in nanoseconds for the last_n matching rows.\n\n    Early dispatches may have inflated times due to warmup effects.\n    Averaging only the last_n dispatches gives steady-state timing.\n    \"\"\"\n    durations = []\n    with open(csv_path, newline=\"\") as f:\n        reader = csv.DictReader(f)\n        for row in reader:\n            if kernel_name in row[\"Kernel_Name\"]:\n                start = int(row[\"Start_Timestamp\"])\n                end = int(row[\"End_Timestamp\"])\n                durations.append(end - start)\n    if not durations:\n        return None, 0\n    tail = durations[-last_n:]\n    return sum(tail) / len(tail), len(durations)\n\n\ndef run_rocprof_trace(version_dir, K, dtype, version, work_dir, env, kernel_type=\"a16w16\"):\n    \"\"\"Run rocprofv3 --kernel-trace to collect kernel timestamps.\n\n    Returns TFLOPS computed from the average kernel time, or None on failure.\n    \"\"\"\n    M, N = 4096, 4096\n    trace_dir = os.path.join(work_dir, f\"{version_dir}_rocprof_trace\")\n    if os.path.isdir(trace_dir):\n        shutil.rmtree(trace_dir)\n\n    cmd = [\n        \"rocprofv3\",\n        \"--kernel-trace\",\n        \"-f\",\n        \"csv\",\n        \"--kernel-include-regex\",\n        version_dir,\n        \"-d\",\n        trace_dir,\n        \"--\",\n        \"python\",\n        \"bench.py\",\n        \"--rocprof\",\n        \"--K\",\n        str(K),\n    ]\n    if kernel_type == \"a16w16\":\n        cmd.extend([\"--dtype\", dtype, \"--version\", str(version)])\n    elif kernel_type == \"a4w4\":\n        cmd.extend([\"--version\", str(version)])\n\n    rocprof_env = env.copy()\n    rocprof_env[\"AMD_SERIALIZE_KERNEL\"] = \"3\"\n\n    print(f\"  rocprofv3: collecting kernel trace for {version_dir} ...\")\n    try:\n        proc = subprocess.run(\n            cmd,\n            capture_output=True,\n            text=True,\n            env=rocprof_env,\n            cwd=work_dir,\n        )\n line in lines[-5:]:\n                print(f\"    {line}\")\n            return None\n    except Exception as e:\n        print(f\"  rocprofv3 FAILED: {e}\")\n        return None\n\n    csv_path = find_kernel_trace_csv(trace_dir)\n    if csv_path is None:\n        print(f\"  rocprofv3: no kernel_trace.csv found in {trace_dir}\")\n        return None\n\n    avg_ns, count = avg_kernel_time_ns(csv_path, version_dir)\n    if avg_ns is None:\n        print(f\"  rocprofv3: no rows matched kernel '{version_dir}' in {csv_path}\")\n        return None\n\n    avg_us = avg_ns / 1e3\n    tflops = 2 * M * N * K * 1e-12 / (avg_ns * 1e-9)\n    print(f\"  rocprofv3: {count} dispatches, avg={avg_us:.2f} us, tflops={tflops:.1f}\")\n    return tflops\n\n\ndef run_benchmark(version, What is MFMA Efficiency?\n\nMFMA efficiency measures how well a kernel utilizes the matrix core. It is defined as the ratio of cycles spent executing MFMA instructions to the total cycles of the main loop, measured per SIMD.\n\nA higher MFMA efficiency means better matrix core utilization. For a compute-bound kernel, the ideal target is close to 100%.\n\n## 2. Why Measure MFMA Efficiency?\n\nTFLOPS is the standard end-to-end performance metric, but it can vary due to factors outside the kernel developer's control—temperature, cooling, system load, and frequency scaling all affect the result.\n\nMFMA efficiency is cycle-based and independent of clock frequency, making it more stable and reproducible across runs. Because it directly reflects instruction scheduling and co-execution behavior, it provides clearer guidance for kernel optimization and compiler tuning.\n\n## 3. How to Measure It\n\n1. **Collect thread traces** using `rocprofv3`.\n\n2. **Process the traces** using the [`process_json.py`](../scripts/process_json.py) script on the generated `ui_` directory:\n\n   ```bash\n   python scripts/process_json.py /path/to/ui_<kernel_name>\n   ```\n\n   The script analyzes `code.json` and wave trace files (`se0_sm0_sl0_wv*.json`) to:\n   - Identify the loop and epilogue boundaries based on instruction hit counts\n   - Compute cycle durations for prologue, loop, and epilogue phases\n   - Count MFMA instructions in the loop and calculate total MFMA cycles\n   - Derive MFMA efficiency as `total_mfma_cycles / average_iteration_duration`\n\n   Example output:\n\n   ```json\n   {\n     \"loop_first_index\": 773,\n     \"epilogue_first_index\": 1038,\n     \"mfma_count_in_loop\": 128,\n     \"total_mfma_cycles_in_loop\": 2048,\n     \"loop_hitcount\": 1016,\n     \"epilogue_hitcount\": 8,\n     \"num_iterations\": 127.0,\n     \"wave_durations\": {\n       \"se0_sm0_sl0_wv0.json\": 456316\n     },\n     \"average_loop_duration\": 456316.0,\n     \"average_prologue_duration\": 2708.0,\n     \"average_epilogue_duration\": 18552.0,\n     \"pro_ratio\": \"0.57%\",\n     \"loop_ratio\": \"95.55%\",\n     \"epi_ratio\": \"3.88%\",\n     \"average_iteration_duration\": 3593.0393700787404,\n     \"mfma efficiency\": \"57.00%\"\n   }\n   ```\n\n   The output includes:\n   - **Cycle ratios** for prologue, loop, and epilogue phases\n   - **MFMA efficiency** within the main loop\n   - **Iteration statistics** for performance analysis\n\n   For deeper investigation, ATT Viewer can visualize thread traces and allow you to zoom into specific code regions. Each kernel's\n30: `bench.py` puts this directory on `sys.path`, so a kernel can simply\n31: `from common import get_pids`.\n32: \"\"\"\n33: \n34: from triton.experimental import gluon\n35: from triton.experimental.gluon import language as gl\n36: \n37: \n38: @gluon.jit\n39: def get_pids(\n40:     M,\n41:     N,\n42:     BM: gl.constexpr,\n43:     BN: gl.constexpr,\n44:     GRID_MN: gl.constexpr,\n45:     NUM_XCDS: gl.constexpr,\n46:     GROUP_SIZE_M: gl.constexpr,\n47: ):\n48:     \"\"\"XCD-aware PID remapping + GROUP_SIZE_M swizzle. Active at any grid_mn.\"\"\"\n49:     pid = gl.program_id(axis=0)\n50:     num_pid_m = gl.cdiv(M, BM)\n51:     num_pid_n = gl.cdiv(N, BN)\n52: \n53:     if NUM_XCDS != 1:\n54:         ## pid remapping on xcds\n55:         # Number of pids per XCD in the new arrangement\n56:         pids_per_xcd = (GRID_MN + NUM_XCDS - 1) // NUM_XCDS\n57:         # When GRID_MN cannot divide NUM_XCDS, some xcds will have\n58:         # pids_per_xcd pids, the other will have pids_per_xcd - 1 pids.\n59:         # We calculate the number of xcds that have pids_per_xcd pids as\n60:         # tall_xcds\n61:         tall_xcds = GRID_MN % NUM_XCDS\n62:         tall_xcds = NUM_XCDS if tall_xcds == 0 else tall_xcds\n63:         # Compute current XCD and local pid within the XCD\n64:         xcd = pid % NUM_XCDS\n65:         local_pid = pid // NUM_XCDS\n66:         # Calculate new pid based on the new grouping\n67:         if xcd < tall_xcds:\n68:             pid = xcd * pids_per_xcd + local_pid\n69:         else:\n70:             pid = tall_xcds * pids_per_xcd + (xcd - tall_xcds) * (pids_per_xcd - 1) + local_pid\n71: \n72:     if GROUP_SIZE_M == 1:\n73:         pid_m = pid // num_pid_n\n74:         pid_n = pid % num_pid_n\n75:     else:\n76:         num_pid_in_group = GROUP_SIZE_M * num_pid_n\n77:         group_id = pid // num_pid_in_group\n78:         first_pid_m = group_id * GROUP_SIZE_M\n79:         group_size_m = min(num_pid_m - first_pid_m, GROUP_SIZE_M)\n80:         pid_m = first_pid_m + ((pid % num_pid_in_group) % group_size_m)\n81:         pid_n = (pid % num_pid_in_group) // group_size_m\n82: \n83:     return pid_m, pid_n\n\n(End of file - total 83 lines)\n</content>","metadata":{"preview":"##############################################################################\n# MIT License\n#\n# Copyright (c) 2026 Advanced Micro Devices, Inc. IN NO EVENT SHALL THE\n# AUTHORS OR COPYRIGHT HOLDERS BE LIABLE FOR ANY CLAIM, DAMAGES OR OTHER\n# LIABILITY, WHETHER IN AN ACTION OF CONTRACT, TORT OR OTHERWISE, ARISING FROM,\n# OUT OF OR IN CONNECTION WITH THE SOFTWARE OR THE USE OR OTHER DEALINGS IN\n# THE SOFTWARE.\n##############################################################################\n\n\"\"\"\nShared Gluon device helpers for the gemm kernels.\n\n`get_pids` (XCD-aware PID remap + GROUP_SIZE_M swizzle) is used by both the\n4-wave (`intra_wave/`) and 8-wave (`inter_wave/`) kernels. Each kernel's\n`bench.py` puts this directory on `sys.path`, so a kernel can simply\n`from common import get_pids`.\n\"\"\"\n\nfrom triton.experimental import gluon\nfrom triton.experimental.gluon import language as gl\n\n\n@gluon.jit\ndef get_pids(\n    M,\n    N,\n    BM: gl.constexpr,\n    BN: gl.constexpr,\n    GRID_MN: gl.constexpr,\n    NUM_XCDS: gl.constexpr,\n    GROUP_SIZE_M: gl.constexpr,\n):\n    \"\"\"XCD-aware PID remapping + GROUP_SIZE_M swizzle. Active at any grid_mn.\"\"\"\n    pid = gl.program_id(axis=0)\n    num_pid_m = gl.cdiv(M, BM)\n    num_pid_n = gl.cdiv(N, BN)\n\n    if NUM_XCDS != 1:\n        ## pid remapping on xcds\n        # Number of pids per XCD in the new arrangement\n        pids_per_xcd = (GRID_MN + NUM_XCDS - 1) // NUM_XCDS\n        # When GRID_MN cannot divide NUM_XCDS, some xcds will have\n        # pids_per_xcd pids, the other will have pids_per_xcd - 1 pids.\n        # We calculate the number of xcds that have pids_per_xcd pids as\n        # tall_xcds\n        tall_xcds = GRID_MN % NUM_XCDS\n        tall_xcds = NUM_XCDS if tall_xcds == 0 else tall_xcds\n        # Compute current XCD and local pid within the XCD\n        xcd = pid % NUM_XCDS\n        local_pid = pid // NUM_XCDS\n        # Calculate new pid based on the new grouping\n        if xcd < tall_xcds:\n            pid = xcd * pids_per_xcd + local_pid\n        else:\n            pid = tall_xcds * pids_per_xcd + (xcd - tall_xcds) * (pids_per_xcd - 1) + local_pid\n\n    if GROUP_SIZE_M == 1:\n        pid_m = pid // num_pid_n\n        pid_n = pid % num_pid_n\n    else:\n        num_pid_in_group = GROUP_SIZE_M * num_pid_n\n        group_id = pid // num_pid_in_group\n        first_pid_m = group_id * GROUP_SIZE_M\n        group_size_m = min(num_pid_m - first_pid_m, GROUP_SIZE_M)\n        pid_m = first_pid_m + ((pid % num_pid_in_group) % group_size_m)\n        pid_n = (pid % num_pid_in_group) // group_size_m\n\n    return pid_m, pid_n","lineStart":1,"lineEnd":83,"totalLines":83,"truncated":false}},"title":"app/repo/kernels/gemm/utils/common.py","time":{"start":1784537380950,"end":1784537380953}},"id":"prt_f7eb77854001HmewqlgMBhtwcR","sessionID":"ses_0814a2b38ffel26EWqZQ2z5Hzx","messageID":"msg_f7eb77656001ZNb2u2sZn4Qfnf"}}
